Worldwide, nearly 40% of <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">pregnancies are unintended</a> (some 80 million unintended pregnancies each year).<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> An estimated 350 million women in the poorest countries of the world either did not want their last child, do not want another child or want to space their pregnancies, but they lack access to information, affordable means and services to determine the size and spacing of their families. In the United States, in 2001, almost half of <a href="/wiki/Unintended_pregnancy" title="Unintended pregnancy">pregnancies were unintended</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Developing_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing world">developing world</a>, some 514,000 women die annually of complications from pregnancy and abortion,<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> with 86% of these deaths occurring in the <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> region and South Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> Additionally, 8 million infants die, many because of <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> or preventable diseases, especially from lack of access to clean drinking water.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">Women's rights</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">reproductive rights</a> in particular are issues regarded to have vital importance in the debate.<sup id="cite_ref-popsearch_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popsearch-279">[279]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>"The only ray of hope I can see – and it's not much – is that wherever women are put in control of their lives, both politically and socially; where medical facilities allow them to deal with birth control and where their husbands allow them to make those decisions, birth rate falls. Women don't want to have 12 kids of whom nine will die." — <a href="/wiki/David_Attenborough" title="David Attenborough">David&#160;Attenborough</a><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> announced a program to reduce its overpopulation by family planning education and putting <a href="/wiki/Women_in_the_workforce" title="Women in the workforce">women in the workforce</a>. It was announced in June 2008 by the Minister of Health and Population <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hatem_el-Gabali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hatem el-Gabali (page does not exist)">Hatem el-Gabali</a>. The government has set aside 480 million Egyptian pounds (about $90 million US) for the program.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup></p>
<p>The business magnate <a href="/wiki/Ted_Turner" title="Ted Turner">Ted Turner</a> proposed a "voluntary, non-imposed" one-child family scenario. A "<a href="/wiki/Population_Matters#Pledge_two_or_fewer" title="Population Matters">pledge two or fewer</a>" campaign is run by <a href="/wiki/Population_Matters" title="Population Matters">Population Matters</a> (a UK population concern organisation), in which people are encouraged to limit themselves to small family size.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_regulations">Birth regulations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_overpopulation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Birth regulations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Overpopulation issue can be mitigated by <a href="/wiki/Birth_control" title="Birth control">birth control</a>; some nations, like the People's Republic of China, use strict measures to reduce birth rates. Religious and ideological opposition to birth control has been cited as a factor contributing to overpopulation and poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sanjay_Gandhi" title="Sanjay Gandhi">Sanjay Gandhi</a>, son of late Prime Minister of India <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a>, implemented a forced <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_sterilization" title="Compulsory sterilization">sterilization</a> programme between 1975 and 1977. Officially, men with two children or more had to submit to sterilization, but there was a greater focus on sterilizing women than sterilizing men. Some unmarried young men, political opponents and ignorant men were also believed to have been sterilized<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Claims neither supported nor mentioned by given source (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. This program is still remembered and criticized in India, and is blamed for creating a public aversion to <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a>, which hampered government programmes for decades.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup></p>
<p>Urban designer <a href="/wiki/Michael_E._Arth" title="Michael E. Arth">Michael E. Arth</a> has proposed a "choice-based, marketable birth license plan" he calls "<a href="/wiki/Birth_credit" title="Birth credit">birth credits</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Birth credits would allow any woman to have as many children as she wants, as long as she buys a license for any children beyond an average allotment that would result in <a href="/wiki/Zero_population_growth" title="Zero population growth">zero population growth</a>. If that allotment was determined to be one child, for example, then the first child would be free, and the market would determine what the license fee for each additional child would cost. Extra credits would expire after a certain time, so these credits could not be hoarded by speculators. The actual cost of the credits would only be a fraction of the actual <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_raising_a_child" title="Cost of raising a child">cost of having and raising a child</a>, so the credits would serve more as a wake-up call to women who might otherwise produce children without seriously considering the long term consequences to themselves or society.<sup id="cite_ref-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg/350px-Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg" width="350" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg/525px-Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c6/Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="407" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Growthbydevelopedvslessdeveloped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another choice-based approach, similar to Arth's birth credits, is financial compensation or other benefits (free goods and/or services) by the state (or state-owned companies) offered to people who voluntarily undergo <a href="/wiki/Sterilization_(medicine)" title="Sterilization (medicine)">sterilization</a>. Such compensation has been offered in the past by the government of India.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014 the United Nations estimated there is an 80% likelihood that the world's population will be between 9.6 billion and 12.3 billion by 2100. Most of the world's expected population increase will be in Africa and southern Asia. Africa's population is expected to rise from the current one billion to three or four billion by 2100, and Asia could add another billion in the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> Because the median age of Africans is so low (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> = 15 years old) birth credits would have to limit fertility to one child per two women to reach the levels of developed countries immediately. For countries with a wide base in their population pyramid it will take a generation for the people who are of child bearing age to have their families.<sup id="cite_ref-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362_285-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362-285">[285]</a></sup> An example of <a href="/wiki/Demographic_momentum" title="Demographic momentum">demographic momentum</a> is China, which added perhaps 400,000 more people after its one-child policy was enacted. Arth has suggested that the focus should be on the developed countries and that some combination of birth credits and additional compensation supplied by the developed countries could rapidly lead to zero population growth while also quickly raising the standard of living in developing countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362_285-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Arth.2C_Michael_E._2010.2C_pp._352-362-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infectious_agents">Infectious agents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_overpopulation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Infectious agents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are also natural diseases, such as <a href="/wiki/Chlamydia_infection" title="Chlamydia infection">chlamydia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonorrhea" title="Gonorrhea">gonorrhea</a> and even some diseases that produce no physical discomfort at all (such as some specific <a href="/wiki/Adeno-associated_virus" title="Adeno-associated virus">adeno-associated viruses</a><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup>) that may also cause sterilization of males and/or females in the population.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> Whereas the natural occurrence of these diseases is not sufficient to significantly reduce the population problem, large-scale production of these diseases and human-induced release of such diseases could quite well be used as a mitigation measure.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extraterrestrial_settlement">Extraterrestrial settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_overpopulation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Extraterrestrial settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Space_colonization" title="Space colonization">Space colonization</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Space_advocacy" title="Space advocacy">Space advocacy</a></div>
<p>Various scientists and <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> authors have contemplated that overpopulation on Earth may be remedied in the future by the use of extraterrestrial settlements. In the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Gerard_K._O%27Neill" title="Gerard K. O'Neill">Gerard K. O'Neill</a> suggested building <a href="/wiki/Space_habitats" class="mw-redirect" title="Space habitats">space habitats</a> that could support 30,000 times the carrying capacity of Earth using just the asteroid belt, and that the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a> as a whole could sustain current population growth rates for a thousand years.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Savage" title="Marshall Savage">Marshall Savage</a> (1992, 1994) has projected a human population of five <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(numbers)#1018" title="Orders of magnitude (numbers)">quintillion</a> (5 x 10<sup>18</sup>) throughout the Solar System by 3000, with the majority in the <a href="/wiki/Asteroid_belt" title="Asteroid belt">asteroid belt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freeman_Dyson" title="Freeman Dyson">Freeman Dyson</a> (1999) favours the <a href="/wiki/Kuiper_belt" title="Kuiper belt">Kuiper belt</a> as the future home of humanity, suggesting this could happen within a few centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Mining_the_Sky:_Untold_Riches_from_the_Asteroids,_Comets,_and_Planets" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining the Sky: Untold Riches from the Asteroids, Comets, and Planets">Mining the Sky</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/John_S._Lewis" title="John S. Lewis">John&#160;S. Lewis</a> suggests that the resources of the solar system could support 10 <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(numbers)#1015" title="Orders of magnitude (numbers)">quadrillion</a> (10<sup>16</sup>) people. In an interview, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hawking" title="Stephen Hawking">Stephen Hawking</a> claimed that overpopulation is a threat to human existence and "our only chance of long-term survival is not to remain inward looking on planet Earth but to spread out into space."<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/K._Eric_Drexler" title="K. Eric Drexler">K. Eric Drexler</a>, famous inventor of the futuristic concept of <a href="/wiki/Molecular_nanotechnology" title="Molecular nanotechnology">molecular nanotechnology</a>, has suggested in <i><a href="/wiki/Engines_of_Creation" title="Engines of Creation">Engines of Creation</a></i> that colonizing space will mean breaking the <a href="/wiki/Malthusian_catastrophe" title="Malthusian catastrophe">Malthusian limits</a> to growth for the human species.</p>
<p>It may be possible for other parts of the Solar System to be inhabited by humanity at some point in the future. <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_A._Landis" title="Geoffrey A. Landis">Geoffrey Landis</a> of <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Research_Center" title="Glenn Research Center">Glenn Research Center</a> in particular has pointed out that "[at] cloud-top level, Venus is the paradise planet", as one could construct <a href="/wiki/Aerostat" title="Aerostat">aerostat</a> habitats and <a href="/wiki/Floating_city_(science_fiction)" title="Floating city (science fiction)">floating cities</a> there easily, based on the concept that breathable air is a lifting gas in the dense <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Venus" title="Atmosphere of Venus">Venusian atmosphere</a>. <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a> would, like also <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Neptune" title="Neptune">Neptune</a>, in the upper layers of their atmospheres, even afford a <a href="/wiki/Gravitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Gravitation">gravitation</a> almost exactly as strong as <a href="/wiki/G-force" title="G-force">that on Earth</a> (<i>see</i> <a href="/wiki/Colonization_of_Venus" title="Colonization of Venus">colonization of Venus</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> authors, including <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_C._Clarke" title="Arthur C. Clarke">Arthur C. Clarke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-clarkebipeds_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clarkebipeds-297">[297]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Asimov" title="Isaac Asimov">Isaac Asimov</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> have argued that shipping any excess population into space is not a viable solution to human overpopulation. According to Clarke, "the population battle must be fought or won here on Earth".<sup id="cite_ref-clarkebipeds_297-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clarkebipeds-297">[297]</a></sup> The problem for these authors is not the lack of resources in space (as shown in books such as <i>Mining the Sky</i><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup>), but the physical impracticality of shipping vast numbers of people into space to "solve" overpopulation on Earth. However, <a href="/wiki/Gerard_K._O%27Neill" title="Gerard K. O'Neill">Gerard K. O'Neill</a>'s calculations show that Earth could offload all new population growth with a launch services industry about the same size as the current airline industry.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/StarTram" title="StarTram">StarTram</a> concept, by <a href="/wiki/James_R._Powell" title="James R. Powell">James R. Powell</a> (the co-inventor of <a href="/wiki/Maglev" title="Maglev">maglev</a> transport) and others, envisions a capability to send up to 4 million people a decade to space per facility.<sup id="cite_ref-StarTram2010_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StarTram2010-301">[301]</a></sup> A&#160;hypothetical extraterrestrial colony could potentially grow by reproduction only (i.e., without any immigration), with all of the inhabitants being the direct descendants of the original colonists.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_overpopulation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Urbanization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite the increase in population density within cities (and the emergence of megacities), <a href="/wiki/UN_Habitat" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Habitat">UN Habitat</a> states in its reports that urbanization may be the best compromise in the face of global population growth.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> Cities concentrate human activity within limited areas, limiting the breadth of environmental damage.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> But this mitigating influence can only be achieved if <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">urban planning</a> is significantly improved<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> and city services are properly maintained.</p>

(1990). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ditext.com/ehrlich/title.html"><i>The population explosion</i></a>. London: Hutchinson. pp.&#160;39–40. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0091745519" title="Special:BookSources/0091745519">0091745519</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">20 July</span> 2014</span>. <q>When is an area overpopulated? When its population can not be maintained without rapidly depleting nonrenewable resources [39] (or converting renewable resources into nonrenewable ones) and without decreasing the capacity of the environment to support the population. In short, if the long-term carrying capacity of an area is clearly being degraded by its current human occupants, that area is overpopulated.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+overpopulation&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul+R.+Ehrlich+%26+Anne+H.&amp;rft.aulast=Ehrlich&amp;rft.btitle=The+population+explosion&amp;rft.date=1990&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ditext.com%2Fehrlich%2Ftitle.html&amp;rft.isbn=0091745519&amp;rft.pages=39-40&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=Hutchinson&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://berkeley.academia.edu/OzzieZehner/Papers/911571/The_Environmental_Politics_of_Population_and_Overpopulation/">The Environmental Politics of Population and Overpopulation</a>. University of California, Berkeley.</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ck12.org/earth-science/Agriculture-and-Human-Population-Growth/">CK-12 Agriculture and human population growth</a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikibooks has a book on the topic of: <i><b><a href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Introduction_to_Sociology/Demography" class="extiw" title="wikibooks:Introduction to Sociology/Demography">Introduction to Sociology/Demography</a></b></i></td>

</table>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://populationaction.org/Articles/Whats_Your_Number/seeandsave.php?date=-14346000000">What's your number?</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Population_Action_International" title="Population Action International">Population Action International</a></li>

Cohen">Joel E. Cohen</a> (43-min video). <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2vr44C_G0-o">The same video</a> on YouTube</small></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/global-development-professionals-network/gallery/2015/apr/01/over-population-over-consumption-in-pictures">Overpopulation, overconsumption – in pictures</a> (April 2015), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i></li>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PUwmA3Q0_OE">Human population through time</a> (November 2016), <i><a href="/wiki/American_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="American Museum of Natural History">American Museum of Natural History</a></i>. Video (6:24 minutes) shows exponential growth of population. "It took 200,000 years for our human population to reach 1 billion — and only 200 years to reach 7 billion."</li>
<li>YAN Kun(2011). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nature.ac.cn/papers/paper-pdf/ConnectionEquation-pdf.pdf">The tendency equation of the population and its limit value in the United Kingdom</a> (Brief annotation of the connection equation(R), p3-p5), Xi'an: Xi'an Modern Nonlinear Science Applying Institute.</li>
